Calculate the amount spent at the supermarket: Total amount - Amount left after visiting the supermarket\n3. Calculate the difference between the amount collected from the ATM and the amount spent at the supermarket\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total amount Olivia had before visiting the supermarket = $3 + $49 = $52\n2. Amount spent at the supermarket = $52 - $49 = $3\n3. "Let's denote the number of baskets with red peaches as R and the number of baskets with green peaches as G. \n\nFrom the given information, we can set up the following equations:\n4R = total number of red peaches\n3G = total number of green peaches\nR + G = total number of baskets\n\nGiven that there are a total of 7 peaches in all baskets, we can write:\n4R + 3G = 7\n\nNow, we can substitute the values of R and G from the equations above into the equation 4R + 3G = 7:\n4(7- G) + 3G = 7\n28 - 4G + 3G = 7\n28 - G = 7\nG = 21\n\nNow, we can substitute the value of G back into the equation R + G = total number of baskets:\nR + 21 = total number of baskets\nR = total number of baskets - 21\n\nSince the total number of baskets must be a whole number, the only possible value for the total number of baskets is 21. Therefore, there are 21 baskets of peaches."

'Let:\nR = number of roses\nO = number of orchids\n\nGiven:\nInitial number of roses = 9\nInitial number of orchids = 6\nFinal number of roses = 3\nFinal number of orchids = 13\n\nWe can set up the following equations based on the given information:\nR(initial) + R(cut) = R(final)\nO(initial) + O(cut) = O(final)\n\nSubstitute the given values into the equations:\n9 + R(cut) = 3\n6 + O(cut) = 13\n\nSolving for R(cut) and O(cut):\nR(cut) = 3 - 9 = -6\nO(cut) = 13 - 6 = 7\n\nNow, we can calculate the difference in the number of orchids and roses in the vase:\nFinal number of orchids - Final number of roses = 13 - 3 = 10\n\nTherefore, there are 10 more orchids than roses in the vase now.'

'Variables:\n- Shirts made yesterday: 9\n- Shirts made today: 8\n- Shirts made per minute: 2\n\nPlan:\n1. Calculate the total number of shirts made in both days.\n2. Calculate the number of shirts made today.\n3. Calculate the number of minutes the machine worked today.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total shirts made = Shirts made yesterday + Shirts made today\nTotal shirts made = 9 + 8 = 17\n\n2. Shirts made today = Total shirts made - Shirts made yesterday\nShirts made today = 17 - 9 = 8\n\n3. "Let's denote:\n- Number of kids Julia played tag with on Monday as M\n- Number of kids Julia played tag with on Tuesday as T\n\nFrom the given information, we have:\nM = 19\nT = 18\nM + T = 19 + 18 = 37 (total number of kids Julia played tag with on both days)\n\nWe also know that Julia spent a total of 38 hours playing tag on both days. Since the number of kids she played with on Monday and Tuesday is directly proportional to the time spent playing tag, we can set up the following equation:\nM*x + T*y = 38\nwhere x and y are the time spent playing tag with one kid on Monday and Tuesday, respectively.\n\nSince the total number of kids Julia played tag with is 37, we can rewrite the equation as:\n19x + 18y = 38\n\nNow, we need to find the values of x and y. Let's solve the system of equations:\n19x + 18y = 38\nM + T = 37\n\nMultiplying the second equation by 18 and subtracting it from the first equation:\n19x + 18y - 18x - 18y = 38 - 18*37\nx = 20\n\nSubstitute x back into the second equation:\n19*20 + 18y = 38\n380 + 18y = 38\n18y = 38 - 380\n18y = -342\ny = -19\n\nSince the number of kids cannot be negative, there seems to be a mistake in the calculations. Let's reevaluate the equations and calculations."

Number of days Debby drank for = Total water bottles drank / Water bottles drank per day\nNumber of days Debby drank for = 144 / 144\nNumber of days Debby drank for = 1\n\nAnswer:\nDebby drank for 1 day.'

"Let's denote the total number of customers as C, the number of customers that left as L, and the number of customers that stayed behind as S.\n\nGiven that the waiter had 11 customers initially, we have:\nC = 11\n\nAfter some customers left, the waiter still had 3 customers, so we have:\nS = 3\n\nWe also know that the total number of customers that left plus the number of customers that stayed behind equals the total number of customers initially, so:\nL + S = C\nL + 3 = 11\nL = 11 - 3\nL = 8\n\nTherefore, 8 customers left and 3 customers stayed behind. To find out how many more customers left than those that stayed behind, we calculate:\n8 - 3 = 5\n\nTherefore, 5 more customers left than those that stayed behind."

"Let's denote the weight of the strawberries Marco picked as M pounds and the weight of the strawberries his dad picked as D pounds.\n\nFrom the information given in the problem, we have the following equations:\n1. M + D = 22 (the total weight of strawberries collected by Marco and his dad is 22 pounds)\n2. D + 30 = 36 (the weight of his dad's strawberries after finding 30 more pounds is 36 pounds)\n\nFrom equation 1, we can solve for D:\nD = 22 - M\n\nSubstitute this into equation 2:\n22 - M + 30 = 36\n52 - M = 36\n-M = 36 - 52\n-M = -16\nM = 16\n\nNow, substitute M = 16 back into D = 22 - M:\nD = 22 - 16\nD = 6\n\nTherefore, Marco's dad's strawberries now weigh 6 pounds."

Money earned during harvest season = Total earnings - Total rent\nMoney earned during harvest season = $94,099 - $11,417\nMoney earned during harvest season = $82,682\n\nAnswer:\nLewis earns $82,682 during the 233 weeks of harvest season."

'Given:\nCrackers = 22\nCakes = 34\nFriends = 11\n\nTo find out how many crackers each person ate, we need to first find the total number of crackers and cakes Matthew gave to his friends.\n\nTotal crackers and cakes = 22 + 34 = 56\n\nNow, we need to find out how many crackers and cakes each friend received on average.\n\nAverage crackers and cakes per friend = Total crackers and cakes / Number of friends\n= 56 / 11\n= 5.09 (approx.)\n\nSince we cannot give a fraction of a cracker or cake to each friend, we need to round down to the nearest whole number. Therefore, each friend received 5 crackers and 5 cakes.\n\nTherefore, each person ate 5 crackers.'

Calculate the total number of seats on all buses by multiplying the number of buses by the number of seats on each bus.\n2. Divide the total number of seats by the total number of students to find out how many seats are in each bus.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total number of seats on all buses = 46 buses * x seats per bus\n2. Total number of seats on all buses = 46x\n3. Total number of students = 92\n4. Number of seats in each bus = Total number of seats on all buses / Total number of students\n5. Number of seats in each bus = 46x / 92\n\nSolving for x:\n46x = 92\nx = 92 / 46\nx = 2\n\nTherefore, each bus has 2 seats.'

'Given:\n- Number of seats on the Ferris wheel: 18\n- Capacity of each seat: 15 people\n- Number of broken seats: 10\n\nPlan:\n1. Calculate the total number of people that can ride the Ferris wheel when all seats are operational.\n2. Subtract the number of people that cannot ride due to broken seats.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total number of people that can ride the Ferris wheel when all seats are operational:\nTotal capacity = Number of seats * Capacity of each seat\nTotal capacity = 18 seats * 15 people/seat\nTotal capacity = 270 people\n\n2. Number of people that cannot ride due to broken seats:\nNumber of broken seats = 10 seats\nNumber of people unable to ride = Number of broken seats * Capacity of each seat\nNumber of people unable to ride = 10 seats * 15 people/seat\nNumber of people unable to ride = 150 people\n\n3. Number of people that can ride the Ferris wheel at the same time:\nNumber of people that can ride = Total capacity - Number of people unable to ride\nNumber of people that can ride = 270 people - 150 people\nNumber of people that can ride = 120 people\n\nTherefore, 120 people can ride the Ferris wheel at the same time.'

Calculate the number of t-shirts sold during the Texas Tech game.\n2. Calculate the total money made from selling the t-shirts.\n\nCalculation:\nNumber of t-shirts sold during Texas Tech game = Total number of t-shirts sold - Number of t-shirts sold during Arkansas game\nNumber of t-shirts sold during Texas Tech game = 95 - 47\nNumber of t-shirts sold during Texas Tech game = 48\n\nTotal money made from selling the t-shirts = (Number of t-shirts sold during Arkansas game * Profit per t-shirt) + (Number of t-shirts sold during Texas Tech game * Profit per t-shirt)\nTotal money made from selling the t-shirts = (47 * $87) + (48 * $87)\nTotal money made from selling the t-shirts = $4095 + $4176\nTotal money made from selling the t-shirts = $8271\n\nTherefore, the Razorback t-shirt shop made $8271 from selling the t-shirts during the Arkansas game and the Texas Tech game.'

Calculate the total revenue from selling t-shirts and jerseys.\n2. Set up an equation using the given information.\n3. Solve for the cost of a t-shirt and a jersey.\n4. Calculate how much more a jersey costs than a t-shirt.\n\nCalculation:\nTotal revenue from selling t-shirts = 254 * (x + $86)\nTotal revenue from selling jerseys = 43 * (y + $232)\n\nGiven that the total revenue from selling t-shirts and jerseys is the same:\n254 * (x + $86) = 43 * (y + $232)\n\nSolving for y:\n254x + $21644 = 43y + $9944\n254x - 43y = $11700\n43y = 254x - $11700\ny = (254/43)x - $272.09\n\nNow, we need to find how much more a jersey costs than a t-shirt:\ny - x = (254/43)x - $272.09 - x\ny - x = (211/43)x - $272.09\n\nAnswer:\nA jersey costs $211/43 more than a t-shirt.'

Let's correct it:\n\n15 - x = 21\n-x = 21 - 15\n-x = 6\nx = -6\n\nThe correct equation should be:\n15 - x = 21\n-x = 21 - 15\n-x = 6\nx = -6\n\nThis means that Dave actually added 6 apps instead of deleting them. Let's correct the equations:\n\n15 + x = 21\n24 + y = 4\n\nSolving the corrected equations:\n15 + x = 21\nx = 21 - 15\nx = 6\n\n24 + y = 4\ny = 4 - 24\ny = -20\n\nSince we cannot delete a negative number of files, we made an error in setting up the equations. Let's correct it:\n\n24 - y = 4\n-y = 4 - 24\n-y = -20\ny = 20\n\nNow, we can calculate the number of apps and files Dave has left on his phone:\nNumber of apps left = 21\nNumber of files left = 4\n\nNumber of apps more than files = 21 - 4 = 17\n\nTherefore, Dave has 17 more apps than files left on his phone."
'Given:\nInitial number of cakes = 173\nNumber of new cakes bought = 103\nNumber of cakes sold = 86\n\nTo find out how many cakes Baker still has, we need to calculate the total number of cakes after accounting for the new cakes bought and cakes sold.\n\nTotal number of cakes = Initial number of cakes + New cakes bought - Cakes sold\nTotal number of cakes = 173 + 103 - 86\nTotal number of cakes = 276 - 86\nTotal number of cakes = 190\n\nTherefore, Baker still has 190 cakes.'
"Given:\n- Sugar needed: 11 cups\n- Flour needed: 6 cups\n- Salt needed: 9 cups\n- Flour already added: 12 cups\n\nTo find:\n- Difference between the cups of sugar and salt needed to be added now\n\nFirst, let's calculate how many cups of sugar Mary has already added:\n12 cups of flour were added, and the recipe calls for 6 cups of flour. So, Mary has already added 12/6 = 2 times the amount of flour needed.\n\nSince the recipe calls for 11 cups of sugar, Mary needs to add 11 * 2 = 22 cups of sugar.\n\nNow, let's calculate how many more cups of sugar than cups of salt Mary needs to add:\nMary needs to add 22 cups of sugar and the recipe calls for 9 cups of salt. Therefore, Mary needs to add 22 - 9 = 13 more cups of sugar than cups of salt.\n\nTherefore, Mary needs to add 13 more cups of sugar than cups of salt."

Calculate the total hours spent on learning English per day: E * D\n2. Calculate the total hours spent on learning Chinese per day: C * D\n3. Add the total hours spent on learning English and Chinese to find the total hours spent on learning both languages.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total hours spent on learning English per day: 4 hours * 7 days = 28 hours\n2. Total hours spent on learning Chinese per day: 5 hours * 7 days = 35 hours\n3. Total hours spent on learning English and Chinese in all: 28 hours + 35 hours = 63 hours\n\nTherefore, Ryan spends a total of 63 hours on learning English and Chinese in 7 days.'

"Let's denote the number of apples Adam has as A, and the number of apples Jackie has as J. \n\nFrom the given information, we have the following equations:\n1. A + J = 12\n2. A + J + 9 = He\n3. A = J + 8\n\nNow, let's substitute equation 3 into equation 1 to solve for J:\nJ + 8 + J = 12\n2J + 8 = 12\n2J = 4\nJ = 2\n\nNow, substitute J = 2 into equation 3 to find A:\nA = 2 + 8\nA = 10\n\nFinally, substitute A = 10 and J = 2 into equation 2 to find the number of apples He has:\nHe = A + J + 9\nHe = 10 + 2 + 9\nHe = 21\n\nTherefore, He has 21 apples."

'Variables:\nZ = number of push-ups Zachary did\nC = number of crunches Zachary did\nD = number of push-ups David did\nE = number of crunches David did\n\nGiven:\nZ = 46\nC = 58\nD = Z + 38 = 46 + 38 = 84\nE = C - 62 = 58 - 62 = -4\n\nWe need to find the difference between the number of crunches and push-ups Zachary did:\nDifference = C - Z = 58 - 46 = 12\n\nTherefore, Zachary did 12 more crunches than push-ups.'
"Given:\n- Number of seats on the Ferris wheel: 4\n- Total number of people that can ride at the same time: 20\n\nLet's denote the number of people each seat can hold as x.\n\nSince there are 4 seats on the Ferris wheel, the total number of people that can ride at the same time is the product of the number of seats and the number of people each seat can hold:\n4 * x = 20\n\nSolving for x:\nx = 20 / 4\nx = 5\n\nTherefore, each seat on the Ferris wheel can hold 5 people."

"Given:\nMoney received from mom = 3 dollars\nMoney received from dad = 6 dollars\nMoney spent = 4 dollars\n\nTo find:\nHow much more money did Gwen receive from her dad than she did from her mom?\n\nLet's calculate the total money received by Gwen:\nTotal money received = Money received from mom + Money received from dad\nTotal money received = 3 + 6 = 9 dollars\n\nNow, let's calculate how much money Gwen has left after spending:\nMoney left = Total money received - Money spent\nMoney left = 9 - 4 = 5 dollars\n\nNow, let's calculate how much more money Gwen received from her dad than she did from her mom:\nMoney received from dad - Money received from mom = 6 - 3 = 3 dollars\n\nTherefore, Gwen received 3 dollars more from her dad than she did from her mom."

"Given:\nPastries made = 61\nCakes made = 167\nCakes sold = 108\nPastries sold = 44\n\nTo find:\nHow many cakes would baker still have?\n\nFirst, let's calculate how many pastries and cakes were sold in total:\nTotal pastries sold = 44\nTotal cakes sold = 108\n\nNow, let's calculate how many pastries and cakes baker still has:\nPastries remaining = Pastries made - Pastries sold\nPastries remaining = 61 - 44\nPastries remaining = 17\n\nCakes remaining = Cakes made - Cakes sold\nCakes remaining = 167 - 108\nCakes remaining = 59\n\nTherefore, baker would still have 59 cakes."

Therefore, we can write the equation:\n\n2x = 14\n\nSolving for x:\n\nx = 14 / 2\nx = 7\n\nTherefore, there are 7 houses in a block."
"Given:\nEd had 22 marbles.\nEd had 6 more marbles than Doug.\nDoug lost 7 marbles.\n\nLet's denote:\nEd's marbles = E\nDoug's marbles = D\n\nFrom the given information, we have:\nE = D + 6\nE = 22\nD = E - 6\nD = 22 - 6\nD = 16\n\nNow, Doug lost 7 marbles at the playground:\nD = D - 7\nD = 16 - 7\nD = 9\n\nTherefore, Doug now has 9 marbles."
"Given:\nDan has $2.\nHe bought a candy bar for $6.\nHe bought a chocolate for $3.\n\nLet's denote:\nCost of candy bar = $6\nCost of chocolate = $3\nInitial amount Dan has = $2\n\nTo find out how much more money Dan spent on the candy bar than on the chocolate, we need to calculate the difference in the amounts spent on the candy bar and the chocolate.\n\nAmount spent on candy bar = $6\nAmount spent on chocolate = $3\n\nDifference in amounts spent = Amount spent on candy bar - Amount spent on chocolate\nDifference in amounts spent = $6 - $3\nDifference in amounts spent = $3\n\nTherefore, Dan spent $3 more on the candy bar than he did on the chocolate."
'Let:\n- Initial number of customers = x\n- Number of customers that left = y\n- Number of customers that stayed behind = z\n\nGiven:\n- After some left, the waiter still had 4 customers: x - y = 4\n- Number of customers that stayed behind than those that left: z - y\n\nFrom the given information, we can see that z = x - y + y = x\n\nTherefore, the number of customers that stayed behind than those that left is x - y - y = x - 2y\n\nSince x - y = 4, we can substitute this back into the equation:\n\nx - 2y = x - 2(x - 4)\nx - 2y = x - 2x + 8\nx - 2y = 8\n\nTherefore, the number of customers that stayed behind than those that left is 8.'

"Given:\nNumber of cakes made = 19\nNumber of pastries made = 131\nNumber of cakes sold = 70\nNumber of pastries sold = 88\n\nTo find:\nHow many more pastries than cakes did baker make?\n\nFirst, let's calculate the number of cakes and pastries left after selling:\nNumber of cakes left = Number of cakes made - Number of cakes sold\nNumber of cakes left = 19 - 70 = -51 (negative because more cakes were sold than made)\n\nNumber of pastries left = Number of pastries made - Number of pastries sold\nNumber of pastries left = 131 - 88 = 43\n\nNow, let's find how many more pastries than cakes baker made:\nMore pastries than cakes = Number of pastries left - Number of cakes left\nMore pastries than cakes = 43 - (-51)\nMore pastries than cakes = 43 + 51\nMore pastries than cakes = 94\n\nTherefore, baker made 94 more pastries than cakes."

Subtract the number of cakes and pastries sold from the initial total to find the remaining number of pastries.\n\nCalculation:\n1. "Given:\nNumber of cakes made = 157\nNumber of pastries made = 169\nNumber of cakes sold = 158\nNumber of pastries sold = 147\n\nTo find:\nHow many more cakes than pastries did baker sell?\n\nLet's first calculate the number of cakes and pastries left after selling:\nNumber of cakes left = Number of cakes made - Number of cakes sold\nNumber of cakes left = 157 - 158\nNumber of cakes left = -1 (This means 1 cake was sold more than made)\n\nNumber of pastries left = Number of pastries made - Number of pastries sold\nNumber of pastries left = 169 - 147\nNumber of pastries left = 22\n\nNow, let's calculate how many more cakes than pastries baker sold:\nDifference = Number of cakes sold - Number of pastries sold\nDifference = 158 - 147\nDifference = 11\n\nTherefore, baker sold 11 more cakes than pastries."

Calculate the number of buses needed by dividing the total number of students going on the trip by the number of seats on each bus.\n\nCalculation:\n1. Total number of students going on the trip = Total number of students - Number of students who don't want to go\n   Total number of students going on the trip = 102 - 22 = 80\n\n2. Number of buses needed = Total number of students going on the trip / Number of seats on each bus\n   Number of buses needed = 80 / 8 = 10\n\nAnswer:\n10 buses are needed to take the trip."

"Given:\n- Matthew had 24 crackers.\n- Matthew gave equal numbers of crackers to his 3 friends.\n- Matthew had 17 crackers left after giving some to his friends.\n\nLet's denote the number of crackers Matthew gave to each friend as x.\n\nSince Matthew gave an equal number of crackers to each friend, the total number of crackers he gave to his friends is 3x.\n\nTherefore, the total number of crackers Matthew had left after giving some to his friends can be represented as:\n24 - 3x = 17\n\nNow, let's solve for x:\n24 - 3x = 17\n-3x = 17 - 24\n-3x = -7\nx = -7 / -3\nx = 7 / 3\nx = 2.33 (approx.)\n\nSince Matthew cannot give a fraction of a cracker, we need to find the nearest whole number. Since he had 17 crackers left, he must have given 7 crackers to each of his friends.\n\nTherefore, Matthew gave 7 crackers to each of his 3 friends."
'Variables:\nLet G = distance jumped by the grasshopper\nLet F = distance jumped by the frog\nLet M = distance jumped by the mouse\n\nGiven:\nG = 21 inches\nG = F + 25\nM = F - 16\n\nWe need to find out how much farther the grasshopper jumped than the mouse, which is G - M.\n\nPlan:\n1. Substitute the given values into the equations.\n2. Solve for F and M.\n3. Calculate G - M.\n\nCalculation:\nFrom the given information:\nG = 21 inches\nG = F + 25\nM = F - 16\n\nSubstitute G = 21 into G = F + 25:\n21 = F + 25\nF = 21 - 25\nF = -4\n\nSubstitute F = -4 into M = F - 16:\nM = -4 - 16\nM = -20\n\nCalculate G - M:\nG - M = 21 - (-20)\nG - M = 21 + 20\nG - M = 41\n\nTherefore, the grasshopper jumped 41 inches farther than the mouse.'

"Given:\nNumber of visitors to Buckingham palace on the current day = 512\nNumber of visitors to Buckingham palace the previous day = 471\nNumber of visitors to Buckingham palace the day before that = 808\n\nTo find:\nTotal number of visitors to Buckingham palace in the past 89 days\n\nLet's first calculate the total number of visitors in the past 3 days:\nTotal visitors in the past 3 days = 512 + 471 + 808 = 1791\n\nNow, let's find the total number of visitors in the past 89 days:\nSince the pattern repeats every 3 days, we can divide 89 by 3 to find the number of times the pattern repeats:\n89  3 = 29 with a remainder of 2\n\nSo, the pattern repeats 29 times with 2 extra days. \nThe total number of visitors in the past 89 days can be calculated as follows:\nTotal visitors in the past 89 days = 29 * 1791 + 512 + 471 = 52,040\n\nTherefore, a total of 52,040 visitors visited the Buckingham palace in the past 89 days."

"Let's denote the number of visitors on the day Rachel visited the Buckingham palace as x.\n\nFrom the information given:\n45 visitors came the day before Rachel visited.\n829 visitors came in the past 85 days.\n\nTherefore, the total number of visitors in the past 85 days can be represented as:\n45 (visitors on the previous day) + x (visitors on Rachel's day) + 83 (visitors in the remaining 83 days) = 829\n\n45 + x + 83 = 829\nx + 128 = 829\nx = 829 - 128\nx = 701\n\nTherefore, 701 visitors visited the Buckingham palace on the day Rachel went to see it."

"Let's denote the number of green peaches in the first basket as x, and the number of green peaches in the second basket as y.\n\nFrom the information given, we know that:\n4 red peaches + x green peaches = 12 (total number of peaches in the first basket)\n4 red peaches + y green peaches = 12 (total number of peaches in the second basket)\n\nSolving the first equation for x, we get:\nx = 12 - 4 = 8\n\nSolving the second equation for y, we get:\ny = 12 - 4 = 8\n\nTherefore, there are 8 green peaches in each basket."

Calculate the total number of houses in all blocks: 78 blocks * 19 houses/block = 1482 houses\n2. Calculate the total number of pieces of junk mail distributed: 38 pieces/block * 78 blocks = 2964 pieces\n3. Calculate the number of pieces of junk mail each house should receive: 2964 pieces / 1482 houses = 2 pieces\n\nTherefore, the mailman should give each house 2 pieces of junk mail.'

Add the number of kids Julia played tag with on Monday and Tuesday.\n2. Add the result from step 1 to the number of kids Julia played cards with on Wednesday.\n\nCalculation:\n1. 13 (kids on Monday) + 10 (kids on Tuesday) = 23 kids\n2. 23 (kids from step 1) + 15 (kids on Wednesday) = 38 kids\n\nTherefore, Julia played with a total of 38 kids altogether.'
"Given:\nArea of the room = 10 square feet\nLength of the room = 5 feet\n\nLet the width of the room be x feet.\n\nWe know that the area of a rectangle is given by:\nArea = Length x Width\n\nSubstitute the given values:\n10 = 5 * x\n\nSolve for x:\nx = 10 / 5\nx = 2\n\nTherefore, the width of Jesse's room is 2 feet."

"Let's denote the total number of bird families living near the mountain at the start as x.\n\nAccording to the problem:\n- 20 bird families flew away for winter\n- 14 bird families stayed behind\n\nTherefore, the total number of bird families after migration is:\nx - 20 (flew away) + 14 (stayed behind) = x - 20 + 14 = x - 6\n\nSince we know that after migration there are 14 bird families living near the mountain, we can set up the equation:\nx - 6 = 14\n\nSolving for x:\nx = 14 + 6\nx = 20\n\nTherefore, there were 20 bird families living near the mountain at the start."

"Let's denote:\n- Number of push-ups Zachary did as Z\n- Number of crunches Zachary did as C\n\nFrom the given information, we have:\nDavid did 36 more push-ups than Zachary: D = Z + 36\nDavid did 33 less crunches than Zachary: D = C - 33\n\nWe also know that Zachary did 58 push-ups and 33 crunches: Z = 58, C = 33\n\nSubstitute the values of Z and C into the equations above:\nD = 58 + 36 = 94\nD = 33 - 33 = 0\n\nThis means David did 94 push-ups and 0 crunches.\n\nNow, let's calculate how many more push-ups than crunches Zachary did:\nZ - C = 58 - 33 = 25\n\nTherefore, Zachary did 25 more push-ups than crunches in gym class today."

Find the difference between the number of eggs and marbles.\n\nCalculations:\n1. Number of groups of 20 eggs = 12 / 20 = 0 (since 12 is less than 20, there are no complete groups)\n2. "Given:\nNumber of cakes Baker made initially = 81\nNumber of additional cakes Baker made = 92\nNumber of cakes Baker sold = 46\n\nTo find:\nHow many more cakes did Baker make than those he sold?\n\nFirst, let's calculate the total number of cakes Baker made:\nTotal number of cakes made = Initial cakes + Additional cakes\nTotal number of cakes made = 81 + 92\nTotal number of cakes made = 173\n\nNow, let's calculate the difference between the total number of cakes made and the number of cakes sold:\nDifference = Total number of cakes made - Number of cakes sold\nDifference = 173 - 46\nDifference = 127\n\nTherefore, Baker made 127 more cakes than those he sold."

So, R - 3 = 2.\n- The tree also has 27 unripe apples. Therefore, the total number of apples on the tree is R (ripe) + 27 (unripe).\n\nFrom the first equation, we can find the initial number of ripe apples on the tree:\nR - 3 = 2\nR = 2 + 3\nR = 5\n\nTherefore, the tree initially had 5 ripe apples."

"Given:\n- Initially, there were 3 snakes and 75 alligators in the cage.\n- 82 snakes and 19 alligators were hiding.\n\nLet's denote:\n- S = number of snakes initially in the cage\n- A = number of alligators initially in the cage\n- Hs = number of snakes hiding\n- Ha = number of alligators hiding\n\nFrom the given information:\nS = 3\nA = 75\nHs = 82\nHa = 19\n\nNow, let's calculate the total number of alligators after the hiding:\nTotal number of alligators = A + Ha\nTotal number of alligators = 75 + 19\nTotal number of alligators = 94\n\nTherefore, there were 94 alligators in total, and the number of alligators not hiding would be:\nNumber of alligators not hiding = Total number of alligators - Ha\nNumber of alligators not hiding = 94 - 19\nNumber of alligators not hiding = 75\n\nSo, there were 75 alligators that were not hiding."
"Given:\n- Total seeds planted = 55\n- Seeds planted in each flower bed = 15\n- Seeds that grew into flowers in each flower bed = 60\n\nLet's first find out how many flower beds were planted:\nTotal flower beds planted = Total seeds planted / Seeds planted in each flower bed\nTotal flower beds planted = 55 / 15\nTotal flower beds planted = 3 with 10 seeds left over\n\nSince we cannot plant a fraction of a flower bed, we can only plant 3 flower beds.\n\nNow, let's find out how many flowers grew in total:\nTotal flowers grown = Seeds that grew into flowers in each flower bed * Total flower beds planted\nTotal flowers grown = 60 * 3\nTotal flowers grown = 180\n\nTherefore, Paige and her mom grew a total of 180 flowers."

"Given:\n- Grasshopper's jump: 13 inches\n- Grasshopper jumped 2 inches farther than the frog\n\nLet's denote the frog's jump distance as x inches.\n\nAccording to the given information, the grasshopper jumped 2 inches farther than the frog. So, the grasshopper's jump distance is x + 2 inches.\n\nGiven that the grasshopper's jump distance is 13 inches, we can write the equation:\nx + 2 = 13\n\nSubtracting 2 from both sides:\nx = 13 - 2\nx = 11\n\nTherefore, the frog jumped 11 inches."
